## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: materials science / solid mechanics (thermomechanical constitutive modeling)
**Analysis**: With sigma as stress, epsilon as strain, and T as temperature, this is a classic stress–strain constitutive relation problem with temperature-dependent stiffness/flow stress (thermoelasticity, thermoplasticity, and thermal softening/hardening effects). The task likely seeks a closed-form sigma(epsilon, T) capturing elastic response, nonlinearity (hardening), and temperature-driven softening or thermal-strain shifts.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear thermoelastic (temperature-dependent modulus): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon (small-strain elastic solid with stiffness varying with T)
- Exponential thermal softening of modulus: sigma = c0 * exp(-c1 * T) * epsilon (stiffness decays with temperature, e.g., near softening regimes)
- Thermal expansion strain shift: sigma = c0 * (epsilon - c1 * (T - c2)) (stress from mechanical strain after subtracting thermal strain)
- Quadratic temperature dependence of stiffness: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T + c2 * T**2) * epsilon (empirical temperature-dependent elastic modulus)
- Nonlinear elastic power law (hardening-like): sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (monotone nonlinear stress–strain curve)
- Polynomial nonlinearity with T-coupling: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon + (c2 + c3 * T) * epsilon**2 (low-order approximation to nonlinear elasticity with thermal effects)
- Exponential strain stiffening: sigma = c0 * (exp(c1 * epsilon) - 1) * exp(-c2 * T) (rapid stiffening with strain, softened by temperature)
- Voce-type saturation hardening with thermal softening: sigma = (c0 + c1 * (1 - exp(-c2 * epsilon))) * exp(-c3 * T) (saturating hardening, temperature-reduced strength)
- Zerilli–Armstrong-like structure (simplified, strain-only): sigma = c0 + c1 * exp(-c2 * T) + c3 * epsilon**c4 (athermal + thermally activated + strain hardening components)
- Johnson–Cook-like structure (no strain-rate term): sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (1 - c3 * (T - c4))**c5 (multiplicative strain hardening with thermal softening factor)
- Entropic/rubber-like scaling: sigma = c0 * T * (epsilon + c1 * epsilon**3) (stress scales with absolute temperature in entropic elasticity, with nonlinearity in strain)
- Smooth elastic-to-plastic transition (tanh blend): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon + (c2 + c3 * T) * tanh(c4 * epsilon) (captures a yield-like transition/rounding without explicit piecewise form)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Temperature softening of stiffness/strength → multiply an epsilon-dependent term by exp(-c * T) or by (1 - c * (T - T0))**n to reduce sigma as T rises
- Thermal expansion effects → replace epsilon with (epsilon - c * (T - T0)) to represent stress-free thermal strain shifting the curve horizontally
- Strain hardening in metals → add a power-law term in epsilon (e.g., + c * epsilon**n) to raise sigma with increasing plastic strain
- Saturating hardening/approach to a limiting stress → use (1 - exp(-c * epsilon)) inside sigma to create rapid initial hardening that levels off
- Rubber/entropic elasticity signature → sigma approximately proportional to T times a strain function, i.e., sigma ∝ T * f(epsilon)
- Yield/transition smoothing without discontinuities → add tanh(c * epsilon) or logistic-in-epsilon blends to emulate an elastic-to-plastic change in slope
- Different thermal sensitivities of elastic vs plastic parts → use separate T-dependent prefactors for linear (epsilon) and nonlinear (epsilon**n or saturation) contributions
- Near phase transitions (e.g., glass transition) → model sharp T-driven changes in modulus using sigmoidal switching in T between two stiffness levels
- Curvature changes in stress–strain with temperature → allow T to modulate the nonlinearity exponent or coefficients (e.g., epsilon**(c0 + c1*T)) to capture evolving hardening behavior
